        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Even after signing Albert Pujols, the Angels have made it clear that they are going to do everything they can to get Trumbos overrated bat into the lineup on an everyday basis. The big boy has impressive raw power, but his refusal to take pitches and draw walks effectively kill his value in OBP leagues. Trumbos value in standard leagues is going to come from his home run total and his positional flexibility. The 26-year-old masher should already be outfield (LF) eligible in your leagues, and if the Halos decide to move him to the hot corner, hell be third-base eligible, as well. If you draft Trumbo for his power and RBI numbers while hoping for a batting average of .265 or better, youre in the right frame of mind. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If you take Trumbo with the expectation of a higher average or above-average OBP, youre doing it wrong. If Trumbo becomes third-base eligible, his value gets a boost that rivals his waistline.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Mark Trumbo may be stuck at designated hitter for most of 2013 -- and there is a slight DH penalty when it comes to their work at the plate -- but hell still have excellent positional flexibility thanks to trials at third base and the outfield in 2012. Trumbo is a monster of a man who can crush pitches into oblivion, but his impatient approach and plodding speed on the basepaths tend to hurt his fantasy value. Hitting .268 with 32 homers makes you a fantasy darling, but getting on base at a below-average rate and crossing home plate a mere 66 times makes you a disappointment. Theres no reason to think Trumbo will change his approach in 2013, but his raw skills will still rank him among the top 12 third baseman. Dont pay too much for this mediocre book with a sparkling cover. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Now a DH, Mark Trumbo will retain third base eligibility in some leagues. Dont pay too much for this mediocre book with a sparkling cover.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Mark Trumbo is now an established 30-HR producer, and with his tremendous power, he's a legitimate 40-HR threat. The move from Anaheim to Arizona is expected to help his chances of improving his home run totals, with a home run park factor for right-handed batters that's about eight percent higher. That translates to an expectation of about two to three extra home runs for him, before you get your hopes too high. He may also be due for a little bit of positive regression in his batting average on balls in play, which was pretty low in 2013 for a man with his power and average-ish speed. His walk rates have risen steadily over the course of his career, and were actually respectable in 2013. Meanwhile, his strikeout rates have gotten worse, as he's gotten worse at making contact on pitches in the zone. He needs to correct the holes in his swing, and needs to take advantage of his power by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/battlefield-trumbo/">hitting more hard fly balls</a>. Easier said than done. But he's an intelligent guy who is <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/mark-trumbo-knows-improves-himself/">aware of his problems</a>, and has shown the ability to overcome them. All told, Trumbo looks like a fairly solid 20ish outfielder or 12ish first base pick, with more upside than downside. (Steve Staude)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Trumbo is a premier home run producer, and a solid 12th pick at first base or 20th at outfield, with more upside than downside. Be careful not to over-rate his move in home parks.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>To some degree you can write off Trumbo's disappointing 2014 season because of a foot fracture that kept him out for two and a half months. However, Trumbo was on pace to have his worst season of his four full seasons in the big leagues. The move from the Angels to the Diamondbacks was supposed to have a positive effect on his already above average power thanks to a more favorable home park, but Trumbo was on pace for the lowest homer total of his career. That's because his home run per fly ball rate rate was only 14.3% compared to 18.8% for his career. The encouraging thing is that his average batted ball distance on home runs and fly balls was in line with what he did in years prior, so it's not unreasonable to expect that HR/FB rate to bounce back. On the batting average front, Trumbo cut down a bit on his strikeouts but hit fewer line drives, so his average remained under .240. If he keeps the strikeout rate down, he could hit closer to .250, but he's not hitting .268 again like he did in 2012. Trumbo's value has always come from his power, and that's where it will come from again this year. Last year's injury should make him much cheaper than he was in drafts last year, but he could still have that 35-homer season in him that a lot of people expected last year in his first year in Arizona. Power is a hard thing to find, and Trumbo could be an under-priced source of it. (<a href="https://twitter.com/TheRealTAL">Brett Talley</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>A foot fracture cost Trumbo two and a half months last year, and he was on pace for the lowest homer total of his career. But his batted ball distance on homers and fly balls was in line with what he had done in years prior, so he may still have a 35-homer season in him. The injury may make Trumbo cheaper on draft day this year than he was last year, so he could be a really nice value.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After a couple of subpar seasons with the Diamondbacks and Mariners, the 30-year-old Trumbo looks to rejuvenate his career in Baltimore. Trumbo has always been known for one trait -- hitting the ball hard, very hard. From 2011 to 2013, he averaged over 30 homers a season. The last two seasons that number is below 20. The drop can be directed at two items. First, he had a stress fracture in his foot, which cost 80 days in 2014. Possibly related to the foot, his rate of home runs per fly ball dropped from a value over 20% to one under 15%. The one noticeable change in Tumbo over the time frame is a drop in the percentage of pitches he pulls over short left field fences. In the second half of 2015, he posted a 39% pull rate which is near his peak seasons of 11 and 12. I wonder if the foot injury messed with his timing. With Baltimore, he gets the luxury of being the full time designated hitter and not being in the field and hitting. I am encouraged and could see a 30 home run season from him with his career .250 AVG. (Jeff Zimmerman)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Mark Trumbo looks to turn around his career after two subpar seasons. If he's healthy, the full-time designated hitter, and playing half his games in home run happy Camden Yards, he could have good value this year.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Trumbo, who could be the poster child for hitting the ball hard and not much else, launched a career-high 47 home runs in 2016. Up to this point, he had averaged ~26 homers a year, making him a solid source of power in all fantasy formats. He has always hit the ball hard since he came into the big leagues (34.9% hard-hit rate for his career). However, during that span he has only had two seasons with offense at least 10% above league average - 24% in 2012, and 23% in 2016 - showing that hitting the ball hard, while desirable, is not enough to guarantee success. Back in Baltimore after re-signing in the offseason, Trumbo should once again be a valuable source of power in all fantasy formats -- even if that is all that he provides. (Joe Douglas)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Trumbo is a great source of power in standard leagues, but he doesn't do much else. While he likely won't top 45 homers in 2017, he should certainly top thirty given a full season.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>

        //            }
        //            else

        hideSO('so6');

        if (panelo.style.display == 'none') {
            panelo.style.display = 'table-row';
            document.getElementById('soa6').style.fontWeight = 'bold';
        }
        else {
            panelo.style.display = 'none';
            document.getElementById('soa6').style.fontWeight = 'normal';
        }
    }

<script type="text/javascript">

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setPost(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_postseason' || node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_postseason_total') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

<script type="text/javascript">
    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
</script>
